## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms

# Envoy Filter Chain Configuration Propagation

## Your Task

Trace how an Envoy HTTP filter configuration defined in a Protobuf `.proto` file in `envoyproxy/data-plane-api` gets consumed by the C++ filter implementation in `envoyproxy/envoy`. Find: 1. The `.proto` file in `data-plane-api` that defines the `HttpConnectionManager` filter chain configuration. 2. The C++ source files in `envoy` under `source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/` that parse and apply this configuration. Report the repo, file path, and key type/class name for each.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` (envoyproxy/envoy)
- `sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367` (envoyproxy/data-plane-api)
- `sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6` (envoyproxy/go-control-plane)
- `sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` (grpc/grpc)

## Summary of Findings

I've documented the complete flow of how HTTP filter configurations propagate from Protobuf definitions to C++ implementation:

**Data-plane-api (Proto Layer):**
- **File:** `envoy/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/v3/http_connection_manager.proto`
- **Key types:** 
  - `HttpConnectionManager` message - Main config container with `http_filters` field (line 471)
  - `HttpFilter` message - Individual filter definition (line 1339)

**Envoy C++ Implementation:**

1. **Config.h/cc** - Factory and configuration classes
   - `HttpConnectionManagerFilterConfigFactory` - Accepts proto and creates config
   - `HttpConnectionManagerConfig` - Processes filters at line 714 using `FilterChainHelper`

2. **filter_chain_helper.h/cc** - Filter processing and instantiation
   - `FilterChainHelper::processFilters()` - Iterates through proto filters
   - `FilterChainHelper::processFilter()` - Creates individual filter factories
   - `FilterChainUtility::createFilterChainForFactories()` - Instantiates filters at runtime

**The Flow:**
1. Proto defines filter chain via `repeated HttpFilter http_filters`
2. Factory creates `HttpConnectionManagerConfig` from proto
3. Config uses `FilterChainHelper` to process each HttpFilter entry
4. For each filter, a factory is retrieved from registry and callback created
5. At runtime, `FilterChainUtility` instantiates filters in order

The answer includes all relevant files, key symbols, the call chain, and a detailed narrative explanation with line numbers and code references.

Draining occurs\n621:   // either when a connection hits the idle timeout, when :ref:`max_connection_duration\n622:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_config.core.v3.HttpProtocolOptions.max_connection_duration>`\n623:   // is reached, or during general server draining. The default grace period is\n624:   // 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds) if this option is not specified.\n625:   google.protobuf.Duration drain_timeout = 12;\n626: \n627:   // The delayed close timeout is for downstream connections managed by the HTTP connection manager.\n628:   // It is defined as a grace period after connection close processing has been locally initiated\n629:   // during which Envoy will wait for the peer to close (i.e., a TCP FIN/RST is received by Envoy\n630:   // from the downstream connection) prior to Envoy closing the socket associated with that\n631:   // connection.\n632:   //\n633:   // .. note::\n634:   //\n635:   //   This timeout is enforced even when the socket associated with the downstream connection is pending a flush of\n636:   //   the write buffer. However, any progress made writing data to the socket will restart the timer associated with\n637:   //   this timeout. This means that the total grace period for a socket in this state will be\n638:   //   <total_time_waiting_for_write_buffer_flushes>+<delayed_close_timeout>.\n639:   //\n640:   // Delaying Envoy's connection close and giving the peer the opportunity to initiate the close\n641:   // sequence mitigates a race condition that exists when downstream clients do not drain/process\n642:   // data in a connection's receive buffer after a remote close has been detected via a socket\n643:   // ``write()``. This race leads to such clients failing to process the response code sent by Envoy,\n644:   // which could result in erroneous downstream processing.\n645:   //\n646:   // If the timeout triggers, Envoy will close the connection's socket.\n647:   //\n648:   // The default timeout is 1000 ms if this option is not specified.\n649:   //\n650:   // .. note::\n651:   //    To be useful in avoiding the race condition described above, this timeout must be set\n652:   //    to *at least* <max round trip time expected between clients and Envoy>+<100ms to account for\n653:   //    a reasonable \"worst\" case processing time for a full iteration of Envoy's event loop>.\n654:   //\n655:   // .. warning::\n656:   //    A value of ``0`` will completely disable delayed close processing. When disabled, the downstream\n657:   //    connection's socket will be closed immediately after the write flush is completed or will\n658:   //    never close if the write flush does not complete.\n659:   //\n660:   google.protobuf.Duration delayed_close_timeout = 26;\n661: \n662:   // Configuration for :ref:`HTTP access logs <arch_overview_access_logs>`\n663:   // emitted by the
